Summary of Manufacturing AI Transformation (AX) Trend Analysis

According to the latest analysis of Manufacturing AI Transformation (AX) trends, AI technology has now established itself as a core driver of innovation in the manufacturing industry. The analysis indicates that the current AI transformation is primarily focused on building 'Smart Factories' and utilizing 'Digital Twin' technology. This signifies a concentration on intelligentizing production processes and simulating them in a virtual environment to find optimal operational methods.

The most notable AI application areas include 'predictive maintenance' for anticipating equipment failures, 'automated quality inspection' through AI vision technology, and data-driven 'process optimization'. Furthermore, the introduction of more autonomous, next-generation technologies such as 'Agent AI' that makes its own judgments and performs tasks, and the integration of 'humanoid robots', is also becoming visible.

While this AI transformation offers significant opportunities for productivity improvement and supply chain efficiency, a shortage of skilled personnel to operate AI technologies, or a 'Skills Gap', has simultaneously emerged as a crucial challenge. For successful AI adoption, strategies that include both technology investment and the cultivation of skilled personnel, along with managing organizational change, are absolutely essential, and through these, we will be able to advance towards future intelligent autonomous factories.

Through Agentic AI, we implement autonomous execution/adjustment beyond analysis in processes, equipment, and supply chains, clearly presenting short-term ROI cases such as quality (vision/multi-sensor), predictive maintenance, dynamic scheduling, inventory/energy optimization, and digital twin integration. For successful adoption, we recommend establishing a high-quality real-time data foundation and MES/SCADA/CMMS/WMS/EMS/ERP orchestration (event triggers, standard APIs, closed-loop control), HITL, and policy guardrails, followed by PoC with KPIs such as bottleneck cycle time, scrap, OEE, and peak power, then phased expansion. Furthermore, a practical differentiator is designing multi-agents to autonomously optimize target metrics by converting OKR/business goals into policies through intent-based automation.

When introducing AI-based sewing and handling automation to apparel manufacturing, start value verification with PoC from bottleneck processes, and standardize equipment/process data and mechanical, electrical, and data interfaces to secure module replacement and line flexibility. If operator-robot collaboration workflows, KPIs (Cycle Time, FPY, Changeover Lead Time), and predictive maintenance and spare strategies are reflected in the initial design, quality stabilization and rapid product changeover can be achieved. Before widespread deployment, minimize vendor lock-in with open APIs and formats, control risks through regulatory and safety compliance, IP protection, and TCO (integration, training, downtime) verification, and implement 'low-manning' lines by expanding the scope of automation for delicate processes like sewing through vision and humanoid integration.

Aitu's AI sewing and modular automation examples demonstrate the potential for reduced workforce and increased line flexibility in apparel manufacturing. This presents a practical roadmap for AI-based manufacturing transformation: reducing risks for new lines and equipment through 4M operational readiness (e.g., personnel competency matrix, OEE baseline, SOP change management). Plant deployment is safely scaled with deterministic networking based on TSN + silicon photonics and leadership operating systems like AAR/Red Team.

This paper presents a practical guide that applies AI-based surrogate models to food and beverage processes, reducing the costs of physical experiments and simulations, while accelerating process parameter exploration and optimization, quality prediction, and real-time decision-making. This review systematically organizes the roles and limitations of AI-based surrogate models in food and beverage manufacturing. The key values are (1) increasing development and optimization speed by replacing/supplementing high-cost physical experiments and simulations, (2) maximizing the return on investment for additional data acquisition through active learning, and (3) presenting a framework for ensuring reliability, including real-time performance and Uncertainty Quantification (UQ), when applying digital twins and predictive maintenance. Practitioners can effectively apply a stepwise approach in the order of KPI definition â†’ data pipeline refinement â†’ DoE + active learning â†’ hybrid modeling â†’ MLOps and model validation.

The core of manufacturing AX in 2025 is to secure E2E visibility by building a digital supply chain/control tower (blockchain if necessary) on a foundation of OT/IT integration, IIoT and RFID-based real-time data, and a standard data model. Building on this, apply AI to predictive maintenance, demand/supply forecasting, and risk simulation; use digital twins to pre-verify the CAPEX, OPEX, and risks of reshoring/nearshoring to optimize layout, automation, and workforce planning; and respond to demand fluctuations and SKU diversification with microfactories. During implementation, simultaneously apply ISA/IEC 62443 security and data/model governance, and enhance field applicability through strengthening connected worker capabilities such as digital work instructions and AR.

Manufacturing 2025 trends are the advancement of smart factories centered around IIoT, digital twins, and AI; the acceleration of reshoring/nearshoring; flexible production based on microfactories; and enhanced E2E visibility. The paper presents, with examples and metrics, how AI and digital social media facilitate business model innovation in advanced manufacturing. Haier's (COSMOPlat) mass customization achievements (35% customized revenue, 30% reduction in production cycle), Sany's predictive maintenance model, among others, are useful benchmarks for practical application. It proposes transforming the revenue model to user co-creation and PSS (servitization) by linking on-site sensor/robot/cloud-based IIoT with social listening, while managing data security, R&D costs, and misinformation risks through governance and a phased roadmap. The effects of AX can be maximized through differentiating data strategies by industry type (process vs. discrete) and KPI-centric maturity management.

As aerospace manufacturing will still depend on human capabilities for approximately 60% of its operations even in 2035, a human-centric AI operating model (two-speed) is key. This model is premised on Human-in-the-Loop, automating repetitive and analytical tasks while humans verify high-risk quality and safety decisions. Short-term ROI areas include supply chain resilience (digital twin, anomaly detection, early risk warning) and MRO predictive maintenance (life prediction, fault classification, material/work optimization). For practical application tasks, prioritize NDT defect detection using Computer Vision, dynamic rescheduling of production lines, and lead time/supplier risk scoring. For success, data and model governance (QMS integration, performance/bias/safety validation, audit logs) must be pursued in parallel with role redesign and upskilling (problem definition, data interpretation, and result verification capabilities).

According to TCS's aerospace AI integration survey, while AI is reshaping manufacturing, supply chains, and MRO across the board, human judgment remains critical in the areas of safety, quality, and oversight. Manufacturers should prioritize human-centric AI operating models (Human-in-the-Loop), supply chain risk monitoring and digital twins, the phased expansion of MRO predictive analytics pilots, data traceability and model governance for regulatory/certification compliance, and upskilling of on-site personnel. In the short term, it is practical to start with applications that have clear ROI, such as automated non-destructive testing, dynamic scheduling, and early warning for delivery risk, and expand from there.

By combining real-time process monitoring with context overlay, Multivariate Statistical Process Control (MSPC), and batch comparison-based Root Cause Analysis (RCA), anomalies can be detected early, decision-making time can be shortened by up to 80%, and defects and stoppages can be prevented. By defining reference trajectories with golden batch modeling, deviation alarms and standard operating procedure consistency are strengthened, and by applying higher-level analytics/recommendation-based optimization without PLC logic changes, implementation risks and downtime can be reduced, and yield can be improved. Furthermore, closed-loop intelligence is predicated on guardrails, approval workflows, safety limits, and OEE/yield/cycle time KPI monitoring, and by connecting operational, quality, and equipment data with integrated batch views and analytics-ready data pipelines, it can be immediately extended to various industries such as life sciences, chemicals, FMCG, and food & beverage.

This content summarizes an AI-based process optimization approach for manufacturing process engineers, presenting methods aimed at improving yield and shortening cycle time through real-time monitoring, multivariate analysis, golden batch modeling, and closed-loop intelligence. The fact that it provides recommendations and notifications at a higher layer without changing PLC logic is a practical point that lowers the difficulty of adoption. However, since specific examples and data are limited, a key insight for on-site application is to collaboratively design data consistency assurance, approval workflow setup, and a KPI-based performance management system.

The 3DFiT single-tow continuous fiber process uses a robot to achieve spatial orientation, including the z-axis, fabricating FCC lattice unibodies at a high speed of 50â€“100 mm/s, reducing costs, lead time, and structural weak points by eliminating joints, and demonstrating performance such as approximately 10% lighter weight compared to commercial products, high specific strength, and an additional 3 minutes of flight time (82 kg payload demo). From the perspective of Manufacturing AX, the core elements are AI path and fiber orientation design linked to stress paths; vision/laser-based monitoring of fiber position, tension, and resin impregnation, and defect detection; closed-loop control of speed, tension, and resin viscosity; and simultaneous optimization of lattice parametersâ€“performanceâ€“cycle time through a digital twin. As implementation checkpoints/KPIs, standardization of scaffolds and anchors, FVF homogenization and porosity management, integration of curing cycles, and cost/lead time reduction management based on deposition speed, fiber orientation deviation, defect rate, UPH, and assembly elimination are recommended.

By combining wireless IoT sensors and AI agents, 'AI-native' batch process automation provides real-time production and quality monitoring and actionable recommendations, proving immediate effects such as reduced cycle time and simplified compliance (e.g., Dr. Squatch). An effective approach involves starting with highly variable batch processes, wirelessly measuring CPP/CQA, providing alerts and recommendations to on-site operators, and automating electronic record-keeping and traceability. ROI can be verified in an 8â€“12 week pilot based on cycle time, yield (FPY), deviation rate, and audit preparation time. To ensure sustained performance, change management risks such as brownfield wireless reliability, sensor calibration, data governance, and alert fatigue must be proactively designed for.

Procense is expanding its process automation platform, which combines wireless IoT sensors and AI agents to collect real-time production and quality metrics and replace manual, sporadic workflows. An early customer (Dr. Squatch) confirmed the effects of shortened batch cycle times and streamlined compliance. For manufacturers in process industries (personal care, specialty chemicals, food, pharmaceuticals), a staged approach is effective, starting with highly variable batch processes to introduce sensor-based monitoring and alert/recommendation insights, then expanding to compliance automation. Results can be quantified by cycle time, yield/deviation rate, and record/audit preparation time, and effectiveness can be enhanced by concurrently designing wireless reliability, calibration, data governance, and change management.

KaizenUp is an AI copilot for manufacturing site managers. Through step-by-step guides and standardized work instructions/coaching, it consistently executes problem-solving, safety (JSA/hazard identification), and training. By connecting on-site proposals from collection to classification and execution with â€˜Quick Kaizen Captureâ€™, it establishes a continuous improvement culture. By integrating with MES/QMS/EHS/CMMS via API, it can automatically connect defect/downtime/near-miss events to the problem-solving workflow, establishing a closed-loop improvement system. With support for closed-source models like Azure OpenAI, it meets data governance and security requirements. For implementation, it is effective to start with a cell/line pilot, set problem-solving lead time, number of hazard/near-miss removals, training lead time, standardized work adherence, and proposal adoption rate as KPIs, and design escalation rules and feedback templates concurrently.

KaizenUp is an AI-powered copilot for manufacturing site supervisors, helping consistent operational improvement by bringing standard problem-solving, risk factor identification, work instruction generation, leadership feedback, and quick Kaizen capture together in one place. Supporting integration with closed-source models and APIs like Azure OpenAI, it enables data connectivity with MES/QMS/EHS, etc., and by training the model with in-house SOPs/standards, improved knowledge reuse and enhanced safety, quality, and training performance are expected. When implementing a pilot, starting on a line-by-line basis and managing problem-solving lead time, number of near-misses/hazards eliminated, training lead time, standard work compliance, and proposal adoption rate as KPIs makes it easy to verify effectiveness and expand adoption.

Presenting a Pharma 5.0 blueprint for pharmaceutical manufacturing, it integrates AI, IoT, digital twin, blockchain, and analytics to detail process optimization (transition to continuous manufacturing, variability reduction), real-time monitoring and predictive maintenance, and enhanced supply chain transparency and data integrity. This review organizes the digital transformation of pharmaceutical manufacturing from the perspective of converging AI, IoT, blockchain, and data analytics, presenting key pillars such as enhanced QMS integrity (eBR, blockchain), digital twin-based process optimization, IoT predictive maintenance, and the transition to continuous manufacturing. In terms of implementation, interoperability, security, regulatory compliance, leadership and change management, and phased pilot implementation are proposed as factors for success and failure. The design of an analysis system through the integration of product/planning/manufacturing data, and a framework for managing performance with KPIs such as OEE, RFT, cycle time, and release lead time, are useful for practical application.

This article presents a method for integrating data silos from heterogeneous systems such as ERP, MES, and IoT into a data cloud and a common semantic layer, and for implementing operational intelligence where conversational and agentic AI performs tasks from evidence collection and inference to action in response to natural language queries. This document presents a practical roadmap for the European automotive transition, and from a manufacturing perspective, it recommends increasing yield and quality through participation in SDV common stacks and shared building blocks, SBOM-based digital threads, MES/PLM integration, and the application of AI in battery cell forming and inspection processes. For critical raw materials such as lithium and cobalt, traceability must be secured through dual sourcing, long-term off-take agreements, recycling design, and digital product passports, and the 'overseas procurement + local production' mix must be optimized through TCO/risk modeling reflecting local content, JV/IP, subsidy, and tariff scenarios. Within the next 1-2 years, the execution of immediately linking regulatory and infrastructure signals (clean transport corridors, charging networks, corporate fleet ZEV transition, toll exemptions) to sales mix, logistics, CAPEX, and workforce retraining plans will determine competitive advantage.

As US power demand grows by 3-5% annually until 2030, driven by data centers (6.7-12% by 2028) and manufacturing reshoring, optimizing location and timing is essential, considering connection backlogs and expansion delay risks in high-growth regions like ERCOT. Manufacturing AX must build a procurement portfolio combining long-term PPAs (renewables + gas backup), DR, and BTM microgrids/CHP/ESS based on Utility IRP, NERC LTRA, and TSP data, and simultaneously optimize cost, capacity, and carbon through peak, cooling, and power density management (reflecting TCO, hybrid cloud/edge) aligned with the AI/OT roadmap.

US power demand is highly likely to enter a period of structural growth, centered around data centers and manufacturing onshoring (3-5% annually). This means that securing power capacity is a key risk and a prerequisite for success when pursuing manufacturing AX. Considering the potential for regional grid connection queues and expansion delays, site selection utilizing IRP and NERC data must be pursued in parallel with procurement strategies (long-term PPA, DR, microgrid/CHP, ESS). With the expansion of gas infrastructure, the effectiveness of CHP and dual-fuel options increases, and following the expansion of AI/OT, phased expansion reflecting power density, cooling, and peak costs in the TCO, and a hybrid (cloud+edge) strategy are recommended.

As demand for wafer processing equipment expands due to increased fab investment in the U.S. under the CHIPS Act and expanding AI/5G demand, a dual portfolio combining leading-edge and mature nodes (approx. 28-90nm) along with investments in digital capabilities such as predictive maintenance, APC, and yield analysis will increase equipment ROI and ramp speed. The U.S. semiconductor manufacturing equipment market is expected to see moderate growth (CAGR 2.9%) until 2033 due to the CHIPS Act and new fab investments. Demand will be driven by AI and 5G, but due to the high proportion of 2D (legacy), equipment and process capabilities focused on mature nodes will continue to be important. To prepare for cost and parts shortage risks, strengthening supply chain resilience through multi-sourcing, strategic inventory, digital visibility, etc., and simultaneously improving ramp-up speed and yield through equipment data, APC, and predictive maintenance centered on wafer processes/foundries are key action points.

The F1/FIA's Siemens NX-based digital twin case is a prime example that, since 2022, has significantly reduced physical prototype and wind tunnel tests and simultaneously lowered lead time and environmental impact by virtually validating over 14,000 CAD parts and 10,000 CFD runs. Manufacturers establish an end-to-end pipeline linking CAD parametric, meshing/CFD automation, HPC scheduling, and PLM data management. While managing performance with KPIs such as virtual validation rate, design iteration cycle, physical test reduction rate, and CO2 per iteration, an effective strategy is to introduce DoE and surrogate models, starting from areas with high physical testing costs, to increase simulation throughput.

Prioritize the adoption of predictive maintenance and computer vision-based real-time quality inspection to secure quick ROI. Continuously monitor equipment and process variations by combining digital twins and real-time data, and transition to planned maintenance. For the supply chain, establish an early risk warning system by linking external data such as logistics, weather, and news. Standardize human-machine collaboration and repetitive task automation with collaborative robots and AI agents to jointly enhance safety and productivity. The core of implementation involves managing performance with KPIs (MTBF/MTTR, defect rate, throughput, changeover, prediction/demand accuracy, energy intensity). Given the AI adoption in manufacturing, with 56% in pilot phases, 20% in scaled operations, and 95% in investment plans, an effective strategy is to prioritize data standardization, governance, security, and HITL verification, and then intensively scale 2-3 high-value use cases such as predictive maintenance, vision inspection, and planning/scheduling. Regarding OT cybersecurity, which has risen to the top ranks of external risks, it is necessary to simultaneously strengthen OT/IT integrated security architecture, network segmentation, and model and data governance. Simultaneously, as demand for power and thermal management facilities rapidly increases due to hyperscaler CAPEX expansion and electrification, there is an opportunity to jointly optimize cost, carbon emissions, and lead time through DR/ESS-based peak management, heat recovery, supply chain diversification, and proactive expansion of production capacity.

The banking sector's shift to 'productive finance', the 150 trillion won National Growth Fund, the 95 trillion won Export and Supply Chain Program, and the spread of AI-based credit assessment will increase access to funding for smart factory, automation, equipment advancement, and supply chain digitalization investments, prioritizing productivity, exports, and value chain contributions over collateral. Manufacturing companies should quantify KPIs such as OEE, defect rate, lead time, and energy consumption, as well as the effects of export expansion and supply chain risk mitigation, in their AX investment proposals. They should also ensure ERP/MES/SCM data consistency and establish a project ROI tracking system to aim for interest rate reductions and increased credit limits. Furthermore, lower implementation risks and accelerate investment speed by linking financial solutions such as working capital + CAPEX packages, supply chain finance based on accounts receivable from partner companies, and a combination of export finance, insurance, and currency hedging when importing equipment.

Following the government-led â€˜productive financeâ€™ initiative, the banking sector will expand funding supply focused on high-tech companies and SMEs, while strengthening support such as interest rate reductions, new loans, consulting, and export/supply chain assistance. In line with the government's comprehensive overhaul of the information protection system, manufacturers must immediately pursue Secure-by-Design (SDL), firmware signing and secure boot, SBOM-based supply chain vulnerability monitoring, and the contractualization of third-party security requirements (SLA) at the production facility and IoT device stages. For OT/ICS, standardize network segmentation, asset visibility, and patch, backup, and recovery training; establish CSIRT, forensics, and reporting systems, premised on the early intervention of regulatory bodies such as KISA; and proactively establish a compliance roadmap focused on model risk classification, data governance, and verification records, utilizing the grace period of the AI Basic Act.

Corelium is an AIÃ—blockchain infrastructure that combines distributed computing, data tokenization, and model monetization/royalties, presenting the possibility of AI cost reduction and data monetization in manufacturing. It can be pilot-applied in a hybrid (on-premise + cloud) manner for non-real-time workloads such as predictive maintenance and quality inspection, and can increase trust in supply chain data sharing with data-NFTs and ZK-based privacy. However, a phased expansion with small-scale PoCs and clear KPIs is desirable while managing SLA, latency, and regulatory risks.

This article points out that generative AI's performance is high in text- and knowledge-centric tasks but limited in physical processes requiring safety, precision, and real-time capabilities, and therefore proposes a phased introduction in manufacturing, starting from document, collaboration, and knowledge management areas. The priorities are automatic generation/summarization of SOPs/work instructions, organizing design change history, internal knowledge-based RAG-powered technical Q&A, and drafting external communications; an approach combining with traditional ML, integrating MES/PLM/ERP and security/audit workflows, and verifying ROI with KPIs such as document processing time, ECO lead time, and onboarding time is effective.

The core of the article is that generative AI shows significant performance variance across industries. In manufacturing, ROI is primarily generated in document- and knowledge-centric tasks (work instructions, design change records, internal Q&A, external communication) rather than in physical process control. Blending with traditional ML, MES/PLM/ERP integration, RAG-based knowledge updates, and the application of human review and guardrails are effective. For pilot projects, it is practical to start with text-dense, standardizable repetitive tasks and to quantify performance using KPIs such as processing time, lead time, and training time.

From a manufacturing AX perspective, this document maps the impact of automation (replacement/augmentation/new creation) based on job roles and tasks across all processes of production, quality, equipment, and logistics, and provides practical guidelines to proactively carry out role redesign and workforce planning based on those results.
